## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws (zero, first, second order, etc.) and more complex mechanisms (Michaelis-Menten, autocatalytic, reversible reactions) govern this relationship.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions, equilibrium shift)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (reversible bimolecular with linear back-reaction)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic growth/consumption)
- Mixed-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface kinetics)
- Time-dependent forcing with first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (time-varying source or coupled species eliminated)
- Combined order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * exp(c2 * t) (concentration-dependent rate with time-varying temperature/Arrhenius)
- Consecutive reaction (eliminated intermediate): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (solution form from coupled linear ODEs)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or effective third-order reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA_dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n
- A polynomial in A for the rate law suggests a reversible or multi-step mechanism with quasi-steady-state approximation
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator polynomials) indicate enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with adsorption
- Explicit time dependence often arises from eliminating coupled species concentrations using their analytical solutions (exponentials in t)
- A rate expression of the form A*(c-A) indicates autocatalytic or logistic behavior with a carrying capacity
- If dA_dt depends on both A and t multiplicatively, this may reflect a temperature ramp through Arrhenius coupling (exp(c*t) factor)
- Sign of leading coefficient determines consumption (negative) vs. production (positive) of species A
- Presence of additive constant terms in the rate law indicates a zero-order source or sink (e.g., constant inflow/outflow)
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) can indicate dissociative equilibrium or half-order kinetics in catalysis
- Exponential decay terms in t multiplied by polynomial in A suggest a mechanism where a catalyst or co-reactant is being depleted independently
